This is the context system ΓÇö one `AppContext` object per request, stored in a `ContextVar` so each thread or async task gets its own isolated slot.\\n\\n## The Core Data Structure\\n\\n```\\nglobals.py\\n  _cv_app: ContextVar[AppContext]   ΓåÉ the single source of truth\\n\\n  current_app = LocalProxy(lambda: _cv_app.get().app)\\n  g           = LocalProxy(lambda: _cv_app.get().g)\\n  request     = LocalProxy(lambda: _cv_app.get().request)\\n  session     = LocalProxy(lambda: _cv_app.get().session)\\n```\\n\\n`LocalProxy` from Werkzeug forwards every attribute access and method call to the live object. The proxy itself is not the object ΓÇö it's a transparent wrapper that re-resolves on each access.\\n\\n## AppContext\\n\\n`AppContext` (`ctx.py`) is the unified context object for Flask 3.x. A single `AppContext` holds:\\n\\n- `app` ΓÇö the `Flask` application instance\\n- `g` ΓÇö a fresh `_AppCtxGlobals()` per context (per-request scratch space)\\n- `request` ΓÇö the `Request` built from the WSGI environ\\n- `session` ΓÇö the deserialized session dict\\n- `url_adapter` ΓÇö the `MapAdapter` used for URL matching and building\\n\\nIn Flask 2.x, there were separate `AppContext` and `RequestContext`; in Flask 3.x they are merged into one.\\n\\n## ContextVar Isolation\\n\\n`ContextVar` (from Python's `contextvars` module) gives each OS thread ΓÇö and each async `Task` ΓÇö an independent slot. Two concurrent requests running in different threads each see their own `AppContext` via `_cv_app`:\\n\\n```\\nThread A: _cv_app ΓåÆ AppContext(app=app, request=request_A, session=session_A, g=g_A)\\nThread B: _cv_app ΓåÆ AppContext(app=app, request=request_B, session=session_B, g=g_B)\\n```\\n\\nThe `app` object is shared (same Flask instance), but `g`, `request`, and `session` are isolated per context.\\n\\n## Push and Pop\\n\\n`ctx.push()` calls `_cv_app.set(ctx)` and returns a token. `ctx.pop()` calls `_cv_app.reset(token)` to restore the prior value. This means app contexts can nest cleanly ΓÇö useful for test helpers and CLI commands that push a context manually.\\n\\n## Proxy Resolution\\n\\nImporting `from flask import request` does **not** resolve the proxy. Resolution happens on attribute access:\\n\\n```python\\nfrom flask import request       # no resolution here ΓÇö import is safe\\nrequest.method                  # resolved HERE ΓÇö reads _cv_app.get().request.method\\n```\\n\\nThis is why proxy imports at module level don't cause circular import problems: the import just names the proxy object; the actual resolution defers to call time.\\n\\n## `g` ΓÇö Per-Context Scratch Space\\n\\n`g` lives on the `AppContext`, so it lives for exactly one request (or one `with app.app_context()` block). It is **not** thread-safe across requests; it is safe within a single request because one worker handles one request at a time.\\n\\nUse `g` to cache data loaded once at `before_request` time and used in the view or helper functions:\\n\\n```python\\n@app.before_request\\ndef load_user():\\n    g.user = db.get_user(session.get(\\\"user_id\\\"))\\n\\n@app.route(\\\"/profile\\\")\\ndef profile():\\n    return render_template(\\\"profile.html\\\", user=g.user)\\n```\\n\\n## Outside-Context Errors\",\n    \"chunk_source\": \"compiled_truth\",\n    \"chunk_id\": 2899,\n    \"chunk_index\": 0,\n    \"score\": 1.2999986827373504,\n    \"stale\": false,\n    \"source_id\": \"default\",\n    \"effective_date\": \"2026-06-11\",\n    \"effective_date_source\": \"fallback\",\n    \"base_score\": 1.2999986827373504,\n    \"evidence\": \"high_vector_match\",\n    \"create_safety\": \"exists\"\n  }\n]"}]}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01SDJVYuazREAXJDtUFhzvws","session_id":"ecdaea3d-793d-427b-9869-5acda3cc8550","uuid":"bfb33af8-6eda-425f-a6df-70488af21bbb","timestamp":"2026-06-17T02:50:04.886Z","subagent_type":"general-purpose","task_description":"Q14-Q25 Conceptual Architectural"}

Every call to `flask.json.dumps/loads` or\\n`jsonify` delegates here at runtime.  \\n- Changing the abstract interface (`dumps`, `loads`, `response`) breaks `DefaultJSONProvider`\\n  and any user-defined provider.  \\n- Changing `DefaultJSONProvider` changes serialisation of all JSON responses including\\n  `jsonify` and the session cookie (indirectly via `TaggedJSONSerializer`).  \\n**Affected:** `json/__init__.py`, `wrappers.py` (json_module), `sessions.py`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### `wrappers.py` (`Request`, `Response`)\\n**Direct impact:** `Flask.request_class` and `Flask.response_class` default to these.\\n- Changing `Request` affects URL rule matching, blueprint detection, form data loading.\\n- Changing `Response` affects `make_response`, session cookie writing, `jsonify`.  \\n**Affected:** `app.py`, `ctx.py`, `sessions.py`, all view functions, testing.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### `sessions.py` (`SessionInterface`, `SecureCookieSessionInterface`)\\n**Direct impact:** `Flask.session_interface` defaults to `SecureCookieSessionInterface()`.\\n- `open_session` is called from `AppContext._get_session()` on first session access per request.\\n- `save_session` is called in `Flask.process_response()`.  \\n- Changing the cookie signing breaks existing client sessions (itsdangerous key rotation aside).  \\n**Affected:** `ctx.py`, `app.py` (`process_response`), all views that use `session`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### `sansio/scaffold.py` (`Scaffold`)\\n**Direct impact:** Base class for both `App` and `Blueprint`. It owns all the hook registries\\n(`before_request_funcs`, `after_request_funcs`, etc.) and the `route`/`add_url_rule` API.  \\n- Changing the data structure of any hook registry (`defaultdict(list)`) breaks `sansio/app.py`'s\\n  `preprocess_request`, `process_response`, `do_teardown_*` which iterate over them.  \\n- Changing `setupmethod` changes when registration is allowed / disallowed.  \\n**Affected:** `sansio/app.py`, `sansio/blueprints.py`, and by extension `app.py`, `blueprints.py`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### `sansio/blueprints.py` (`Blueprint`, `BlueprintSetupState`)\\n**Direct impact:** `BlueprintSetupState.add_url_rule` is the bridge from blueprint-relative\\nrules to `Flask.add_url_rule`. Changing prefix/subdomain resolution logic here changes how\\nall blueprint routes are mounted.  \\n**Affected:** `blueprints.py`, `app.py` (`register_blueprint`), every app that uses blueprints.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### `sansio/app.py` (`App`)\\n**Direct impact:** `App` owns the URL map (`werkzeug.routing.Map`), the blueprint registry,\\nthe Jinja env, the JSON provider, the logger, and many config-derived properties.  \\n- Changes to `create_url_adapter`, `iter_blueprints`, `update_template_context`, or\\n  `add_url_rule` propagate to every request handled.  \\n**Affected:** `app.py` (Flask inherits), `templating.py` (uses `app.iter_blueprints`),\\n`ctx.py` (uses `app.create_url_adapter`).\\n\\n---\\n\\n### `ctx.py` (`AppContext`)\\n**Direct impact:** The unified context object pushed for every request and CLI command.\\nHolds `g`, `request`, `session`, `url_adapter`.\\n- `push()` / `pop()` must remain a matched pair; any change to teardown ordering here changes\\n  when `teardown_request_funcs` and `teardown_appcontext_funcs` run.  \\n- Merging request+app context (Flask 3.2) means `has_request` must be checked before accessing\\n  `ctx.request`; code that assumes context is always a request context will break.  \\n**Affected:** `app.py` (wsgi_app, full_dispatch_request), `globals.py` (proxies), `helpers.py`\\n(`after_this_request`, `copy_current_request_context`), `templating.py`.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### `templating.py` (`DispatchingJinjaLoader`, `Environment`)\\n**Direct impact:**\\n- `DispatchingJinjaLoader` iterates `app.iter_blueprints()` to resolve templates. Adding or\\n  removing blueprint Jinja loaders here changes template resolution order.\\n- `_default_template_ctx_processor` injects `g` and `request` into every template context.\\n  Removing it breaks templates that reference `{{ g }}` or `{{ request }}`.  \\n**Affected:** `sansio/scaffold.py` (registers the ctx processor), `sansio/app.py` (creates the\\nJinja env), every template rendered by the app.\\n\\n---\",\n    \"chunk_source\": \"compiled_truth\",\n    \"chunk_id\": 2764,\n    \"chunk_index\": 6,\n    \"score\": 0.999943733215332,\n    \"stale\": false,\n    \"source_id\": \"default\",\n    \"effective_date\": \"2026-06-09\",\n    \"effective_date_source\": \"fallback\",\n    \"base_score\": 0.999943733215332,\n    \"evidence\": \"high_vector_match\",\n    \"create_safety\": \"exists\"\n  }\n]"}]}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01SDJVYuazREAXJDtUFhzvws","session_id":"ecdaea3d-793d-427b-9869-5acda3cc8550","uuid":"5dbcf1e8-9a05-4ba9-90b8-03ae3b2a06a9","timestamp":"2026-06-17T02:50:10.613Z","subagent_type":"general-purpose","task_description":"Q14-Q25 Conceptual Architectural"}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_016898yGFPVo84US3w2ZsRnj","type":"tool_result","content":[{"type":"text","text":"[\n  {\n    \"slug\": \"context/docs/reference-core-api\",\n    \"page_id\": 307,\n    \"title\": \"Core API Reference\",\n    \"type\": \"note\",\n    \"chunk_text\": \"Prevents path traversal attacks by\\nrefusing to serve paths that would escape `directory`.\\n\\n```python\\nreturn send_from_directory(\\\"uploads\\\", filename)\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n### `stream_with_context(generator_or_function)`\\n\\nWrap a response generator so it runs inside the current request context, keeping\\n`request`, `session`, and `g` accessible even after the view function returns.\\n\\n```python\\n@app.get(\\\"/stream\\\")\\ndef streamed():\\n    @stream_with_context\\n    def generate():\\n        yield \\\"chunk1\\\"\\n        yield request.args[\\\"name\\\"]  # request is still available\\n    return Response(generate())\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n### `get_flashed_messages(with_categories=False, category_filter=())`\\n\\nReturn and remove messages stored by `flash()`. Usually called in templates.\\n\\n---\\n\\n### `has_request_context()` / `has_app_context()`\\n\\nReturn `True` if a request context or app context is currently active.\\nUse to write code that works both inside and outside of a request.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Signals\\n\\nFlask emits signals (via [blinker](https://blinker.readthedocs.io/)) at key\\npoints in the request lifecycle. Subscribe with `.connect(receiver)`.\\n\\n| Signal | Sent when | Sender | Extra kwargs |\\n|---|---|---|---|\\n| `request_started` | Request context pushed, before dispatch | `app` | ΓÇö |\\n| `request_finished` | After successful dispatch, before response sent | `app` | `response` |\\n| `request_tearing_down` | Request context torn down | `app` | `exc` |\\n| `got_request_exception` | An exception is raised during dispatch | `app` | `exception` |\\n| `appcontext_pushed` | App context pushed | `app` | ΓÇö |\\n| `appcontext_popped` | App context popped | `app` | `exc` |\\n| `appcontext_tearing_down` | App context being torn down | `app` | `exc` |\\n| `before_render_template` | Before a template is rendered | `app` | `template`, `context` |\\n| `template_rendered` | After a template is rendered | `app` | `template`, `context` |\\n| `message_flashed` | A message is flashed | `app` | `message`, `category` |\\n\\n```python\\nfrom flask import request_finished\\n\\ndef log_response(sender, response, **extra):\\n    sender.logger.info(f\\\"{response.status_code} {request.path}\\\")\\n\\nrequest_finished.connect(log_response, app)\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Class-Based Views\\n\\n### `View`\\n\\nBase class for class-based views. Override `dispatch_request` to handle all\\nmethods, or set `methods` to restrict which HTTP methods the view accepts.\\n\\n```python\\nfrom flask.views import View\\n\\nclass UserView(View):\\n    methods = [\\\"GET\\\"]\\n\\n    def dispatch_request(self, user_id):\\n        user = db.get_or_404(User, user_id)\\n        return render_template(\\\"user.html\\\", user=user)\\n\\napp.add_url_rule(\\\"/users/<int:user_id>\\\", view_func=UserView.as_view(\\\"user\\\"))\\n```\\n\\n**Class attributes**\\n\\n| Attribute | Type | Default | Description |\\n|---|---|---|---|\\n| `methods` | `Collection[str] \\\\| None` | `None` | HTTP methods this view accepts |\\n| `decorators` | `list[Callable]` | `[]` | Decorators applied to the generated view function |\\n| `init_every_request` | `bool` | `True` | Create a new view instance per request. Set to `False` for efficiency if `self` is read-only |\\n\\n### `MethodView`\\n\\nSubclass of `View` that routes HTTP methods to same-named methods (`get`, `post`,\\n`put`, `delete`, `patch`).\\n\\n```python\\nfrom flask.views import MethodView\\n\\nclass ItemAPI(MethodView):\\n    def get(self, item_id):\\n        return jsonify(db.get_or_404(Item, item_id).to_dict())\\n\\n    def put(self, item_id):\\n        item = db.get_or_404(Item, item_id)\\n        item.update(request.json)\\n        db.session.commit()\\n        return jsonify(item.to_dict())\\n\\n    def delete(self, item_id):\\n        item = db.get_or_404(Item, item_id)\\n        db.session.delete(item)\\n        db.session.commit()\\n        return \\\"\\\", 204\\n\\napp.add_url_rule(\\\"/items/<int:item_id>\\\", view_func=ItemAPI.as_view(\\\"item_api\\\"))\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Related\\n\\n- [Configuration Reference](reference-configuration.md) ΓÇö every config key\\n- [Contexts and Proxies](explanation-contexts-and-proxies.md) ΓÇö how `request`, `g`, `current_app` work\\n- [How to organize with Blueprints](howto-blueprints.md)\\n- [How to write tests](howto-testing.md)\",\n    \"chunk_source\": \"compiled_truth\",\n    \"chunk_id\": 2710,\n    \"chunk_index\": 4,\n    \"score\": 0.9999999403953552,\n    \"stale\": false,\n    \"source_id\": \"default\",\n    \"effective_date\": \"2026-06-09\",\n    \"effective_date_source\": \"fallback\",\n    \"base_score\": 0.9999999403953552,\n    \"evidence\": \"high_vector_match\",\n    \"create_safety\": \"exists\"\n  },\n  {\n    \"slug\": \"context/docs/knowledge-graph\",\n    \"page_id\": 309,\n    \"title\": \"Flask Codebase Knowledge Graph\",\n    \"type\": \"note\",\n    \"chunk_text\": \"# Flask Codebase Knowledge Graph\\n\\nGenerated by static analysis + code reading of `src/flask/`.  \\nLSP (Python) was unavailable; relationships derived from imports, class hierarchies, and call-site reading.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## 1. Module Dependency Map\\n\\n### Notation\\n```\\nA ΓåÆ imports ΓåÆ B          (A depends on B at runtime)\\nA ΓåÆ type-only ΓåÆ B        (A imports B inside TYPE_CHECKING only)\\nA ΓåÆ extends ΓåÆ B          (class inheritance)\\nA ΓåÆ calls ΓåÆ B.func()     (direct call to function or method)\\nA ΓåÆ emits ΓåÆ Signal       (sends a blinker signal)\\nSignal ΓåÆ consumed by ΓåÆ A (A connects to the signal)\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n### `typing.py`\\nPure type-alias module; no flask-internal runtime imports.\\n\\n```\\ntyping.py ΓåÆ imports ΓåÆ (stdlib only: collections.abc, typing)\\ntyping.py ΓåÆ sansio/ Pattern\\n\\nThe `sansio/` directory contains modules with no WSGI knowledge and no I/O:\\n\\n- **`sansio/scaffold.py`** ΓÇö URL rule + hook decorator registry, static file config\\n- **`sansio/app.py`** ΓÇö URL map, blueprint registry, Jinja environment, JSON provider, logger\\n- **`sansio/blueprints.py`** ΓÇö deferred function accumulation, `BlueprintSetupState`\\n\\nThe concrete WSGI layer (`app.py`, `ctx.py`) adds the request handling, ContextVar management, and `run()` on top.\\n\\n## Signal Emission Map\\n\\n| Signal | Emitter | When |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| `request_started` | `Flask.full_dispatch_request` | Before before_request hooks |\\n| `request_finished` | `Flask.finalize_request` | After response built, before teardown |\\n| `request_tearing_down` | `Flask.do_teardown_request` | After request context torn down |\\n| `got_request_exception` | `Flask.handle_user_exception` | On any unhandled exception |\\n| `appcontext_tearing_down` | When `flash()` is called |\\n\\n## Impact Analysis\\n\\n**Highest impact** ΓÇö changes break the whole request pipeline:\\n\\n- **`globals.py` / `_cv_app`** ΓÇö every proxy depends on this ContextVar; changing its type or name breaks all proxies in all modules\\n- **`app.py` (Flask)** ΓÇö owns the entire WSGI lifecycle; method signature changes break subclasses and extensions\\n- **`sansio/scaffold.py`** ΓÇö data structure changes to hook registries (`before_request_funcs`, etc.) break `preprocess_request`, `process_response`, and all teardown logic\\n\\n**Session data stability:**\\n\\n- **`json/tag.py`** ΓÇö adding or removing a tag class changes the session cookie wire format; existing sessions become unreadable\\n- **`sessions.py`** ΓÇö changing the signing It is passed the name of the module or package of the\n112\t    application.  Once it is created it will act as a central registry for\n113\t    the view functions, the URL rules, template configuration and much more.\n114\t\n115\t    The name of the package is used to resolve resources from inside the\n116\t    package or the folder the module is contained in depending on if the\n117\t    package parameter resolves to an actual python package (a folder with\n118\t    an :file:`__init__.py` file inside) or a standard module (just a ``.py`` file).\n119\t\n120\t    For more information about resource loading, see :func:`open_resource`.\n121\t\n122\t    Usually you create a :class:`Flask` instance in your main module or\n123\t    in the :file:`__init__.py` file of your package like this::\n124\t\n125\t        from flask import Flask\n126\t        app = Flask(__name__)\n127\t\n128\t    .. admonition:: About the First Parameter\n129\t\n130\t        The idea of the first parameter is to give Flask an idea of what\n131\t        belongs to your application.  This name is used to find resources\n132\t        on the filesystem, can be used by extensions to improve debugging\n133\t        information and a lot more.\n134\t\n135\t        So it's important what you provide there.  If you are using a single\n136\t        module, `__name__` is always the correct value.  If you however are\n137\t        using a package, it's usually recommended to hardcode the name of\n138\t        your package there.\n139\t\n140\t        For example if your application is defined in :file:`yourapplication/app.py`\n141\t        you should create it with one of the two versions below::\n142\t\n143\t            app = Flask('yourapplication')\n144\t            app = Flask(__name__.split('.')[0])\n145\t\n146\t        Why is that?  The application will work even with `__name__`, thanks\n147\t        to how resources are looked up.  However it will make debugging more\n148\t        painful.  Certain extensions can make assumptions based on the\n149\t        import name of your application. If the import name is not properly set\n152\t        up, that debugging information is lost. Subdomain\n172\t       matching needs to be enabled manually now. Relative to the application ``root_path``\n181\t        or an absolute path. Defaults to ``'static'``.\n182\t    :param static_host: the host to use when adding the static route.\n183\t        Defaults to None. This keeps :data:`.request`, :data:`.session`, and :data:`.g`\n68\t    available, even though at the point the generator runs the request context\n69\t    will typically have ended.\n70\t\n71\t    .. warning::\n72\t\n73\t        Due to the following caveat, it is often safer to pass the data you\n74\t        need as arguments to the generator, rather than relying on the context\n75\t        objects.\n76\t\n77\t    More headers cannot be sent after the body has begun. In particular,\n79\t    if the generator will access ``session``, be sure to do so in the view as\n80\t    well so that the ``Vary: cookie`` header will be set. Do not modify the\n81\t    session in the generator, as the ``Set-Cookie`` header will already be sent.\n82\t\n83\t    Use it as a decorator on a generator function:\n84\t\n85\t    .. code-block:: python\n86\t\n87\t        from flask import stream_with_context, request, Response\n88\t\n89\t        @app.get(\"/stream\")\n90\t        def streamed_response():\n91\t            @stream_with_context\n92\t            def generate():\n93\t                yield \"Hello \"\n94\t                yield request.args[\"name\"]\n95\t                yield \"!\"\n96\t\n97\t            return Response(generate())\n98\t\n99\t    Or use it as a wrapper around a created generator:\n100\t\n101\t    .. code-block:: python\n102\t\n103\t        from flask import stream_with_context, request, Response\n104\t\n105\t        @app.get(\"/stream\")\n106\t        def streamed_response():\n107\t            def generate():\n108\t                yield \"Hello \"\n109\t                yield request.args[\"name\"]\n110\t                yield \"!\"\n111\t\n112\t            return Response(stream_with_context(generate()))\n113\t\n114\t    .. versionadded:: 0.9\n115\t    \"\"\"\n116\t    try:\n117\t        gen = iter(generator_or_function)  # By default just the messages are returned,\n366\t    but when `with_categories` is set to ``True``, the return value will\n367\t    be a list of tuples in the form ``(category, message)`` instead.\n368\t\n369\t    Filter the flashed messages to one or more categories by providing those\n370\t    categories in `category_filter`.  This allows rendering categories in\n371\t    separate html blocks.  The `with_categories` and `category_filter`\n372\t    arguments are distinct:\n373\t\n374\t    * `with_categories` controls whether categories are returned with message\n375\t      text (``True`` gives a tuple, where ``False`` gives just the message text).\n376\t    * `category_filter` filters the messages down to only those matching the\n377\t      provided categories.\n378\t\n379\t    See :doc:`/patterns/flashing` for examples.\n380\t\n381\t    .. versionchanged:: 0.3\n382\t       `with_categories` parameter added.\n383\t\n384\t    .. versionchanged:: 0.9\n385\t        `category_filter` parameter added.\n386\t\n387\t    :param with_categories: set to ``True`` to also receive categories.\n388\t    :param category_filter: filter of categories to limit return values. Paths\n430\t    are preferred in most cases because Werkzeug can manage the file and\n431\t    get extra information from the path. Passing a file-like object\n432\t    requires that the file is opened in binary mode, and is mostly\n433\t    useful when building a file in memory with :class:`io.BytesIO`.\n434\t\n435\t    Never pass file paths provided by a user. The path is assumed to be\n436\t    trusted, so a user could craft a path to access a file you didn't\n437\t    intend. Use :func:`send_from_directory` to safely serve\n438\t    user-requested paths from within a directory.\n439\t\n440\t    If the WSGI server sets a ``file_wrapper`` in ``environ``, it is\n441\t    used, otherwise Werkzeug's built-in wrapper is used. Alternatively,\n442\t    if the HTTP server supports ``X-Sendfile``, configuring Flask with\n443\t    ``USE_X_SENDFILE = True`` will tell the server to send the given\n444\t    path, which is much more efficient than reading it in Python.\n445\t\n446\t    :param path_or_file: The path to the file to send, relative to the\n447\t        current working directory if a relative path is given.\n448\t        Alternatively, a file-like object opened in binary mode. Make\n449\t        sure the file pointer is seeked to the start of the data.\n450\t    :param mimetype: The MIME type to send for the file. There are two common patterns to populate the\n53\t    config.\n54\t\n55\t    Either you can fill the config from a config file::\n56\t\n57\t        app.config.from_pyfile('yourconfig.cfg')\n58\t\n59\t    Or alternatively you can define the configuration options in the\n60\t    module that calls :meth:`from_object` or provide an import path to\n61\t    a module that should be loaded. This makes it possible to use\n71\t    lowercase values in the config file for temporary values that are not added\n72\t    to the config or to define the config keys in the same file that implements\n73\t    the application.\n74\t\n75\t    Probably the most interesting way to load configurations is from an\n76\t    environment variable pointing to a file::\n77\t\n78\t        app.config.from_envvar('YOURAPPLICATION_SETTINGS')\n79\t\n80\t    In this case before launching the application you have to set this\n81\t    environment variable to the file you want to use. Values\n131\t        are passed through a loading function to attempt to convert them\n132\t        to more specific types than strings.\n133\t\n134\t        Keys are loaded in :func:`sorted` order.\n135\t\n136\t        The default loading function attempts to parse values as any\n137\t        valid JSON type, including dicts and lists.\n138\t\n139\t        Specific items in nested dicts can be set by separating the\n140\t        keys with double underscores (``__``). If an intermediate key\n141\t        doesn't exist, it will be initialized to an empty dict.\n142\t\n143\t        :param prefix: Load env vars that start with this prefix,\n144\t            separated with an underscore (``_``).\n145\t        :param loads: Pass each string value to this function and use\n146\t            the returned value as the config value. If any error is\n147\t            raised it is ignored and the value remains a string. Jinja template globals are set to `self.url_for` at `app.py:496`.\n6. **Changing `create_jinja_environment`** ΓÇö breaks `templating.py` `Environment` and `DispatchingJinjaLoader`.\n7. **Changing `app_context()` / `request_context()`** ΓÇö breaks `AppContext` creation, tearing down all context-dependent code in `ctx.py`, `helpers.py`, `templating.py`.\n8. **Changing `session_interface`** ΓÇö breaks `sessions.py` `SecureCookieSessionInterface`.\n9. **Changing `teardown_appcontext_funcs`** ΓÇö breaks `do_teardown_appcontext` and all registered teardown functions.\n10. **Changing `response_class` / `request_class`** ΓÇö breaks `wrappers.py` `Request`/`Response`.\n\n**Total files in blast radius: ~15 source files + all test files (30+) + all example apps.**\n\n---\n\n## Q27. Functions/Methods That Call `AppContext.push()`\n\n`AppContext.push()` is defined at `src/flask/ctx.py:416`.\n\n| Caller | File | Line | Mechanism |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `AppContext.__enter__` | `src/flask/ctx.py` | 507 | `self.push()` ΓÇö called by `with ctx:` blocks |\n| `Flask.wsgi_app` | `src/flask/app.py` | 1596 | `ctx.push()` ΓÇö called directly at start of every HTTP request |\n\n**Transitively triggered by:**\n- `Flask.app_context()` returns an `AppContext`; users call `with app.app_context(): ...` which calls `__enter__` ΓåÆ `push()`.\n- `Flask.request_context(environ)` returns `AppContext.from_environ(app, environ)`.\n- `Flask.test_request_context(...)` creates and returns an `AppContext` via `request_context`.\n- `stream_with_context` in `helpers.py:133` uses `with ctx:` on an existing context, re-triggering `__enter__` ΓåÆ `push()`.\n- `copy_current_request_context` wrapper in `ctx.py:203` uses `with original.copy() as ctx:`.\n\n---\n\n## Q31. Blast Radius of Changing `RequestContext` or `AppContext`\n\nAs of Flask 3.2, `RequestContext` was merged into `AppContext` (the alias `RequestContext` now raises a `DeprecationWarning` and returns `AppContext`, see `ctx.py:528ΓÇô540`). The analysis below covers `AppContext`.\n\n**Files that directly depend on `AppContext`:**\n\n| File | How | What breaks |\n|---|---|---|\n| `src/flask/app.py:33` | `from .ctx import AppContext` | All WSGI entry points: `wsgi_app`, `request_context`, `app_context`, `test_request_context`, all `ctx:`-typed method signatures (`handle_exception`, `dispatch_request`, etc.) |\n| `src/flask/globals.py:11` | TYPE_CHECKING `from .ctx import AppContext` | `_cv_app: ContextVar[AppContext]`, `app_ctx`, `current_app`, `g`, `request`, `session` proxies |\n| `src/flask/templating.py:10` | `from .ctx import AppContext` | `_render`, `render_template`, `render_template_string`, `stream_template*` all accept `ctx: AppContext` |\n| `src/flask/sansio/app.py:23` | `from ..ctx import _AppCtxGlobals` | `App.app_ctx_globals_class`, `do_teardown_appcontext` |\n| `src/flask/__init__.py:5-8` | Re-exports `after_this_request`, `copy_current_request_context`, `has_app_context`, `has_request_context` | Public API breakage |\n\n**Indirect dependents (hop 2 ΓÇö anything using `current_app`, `g`, `request`, `session`):**\n- `src/flask/helpers.py` ΓÇö `flash`, `get_flashed_messages`, `url_for`, `send_file`, `redirect`, `abort` all access context globals.\n- `src/flask/views.py` ΓÇö `View.dispatch_request` uses `request`.\n- `src/flask/wrappers.py` ΓÇö `current_app` used for JSON provider.\n- `src/flask/blueprints.py` ΓÇö `current_app` for config access.\n- `src/flask/cli.py` ΓÇö `current_app` for CLI commands.\n- `src/flask/json/__init__.py` ΓÇö `current_app` for JSON serialization.\n- `src/flask/logging.py` ΓÇö `request` for log formatting.\n\n**Total: ~13 source files directly or 1 hop away; entire public API (via `__init__.py`) at hop 2.**\n\nChanging `AppContext.__init__`, `push()`, `pop()`, `has_request`, `request`, `session`, or `g` would cascade failures across the entire request lifecycle.\n\n---\n\n## Q32. What Calls `teardown_appcontext` ΓÇö Full Trigger Chain\n\n`teardown_appcontext` is the **decorator** defined at `src/flask/sansio/app.py:827`. It appends functions to `self.teardown_appcontext_funcs` (line 854).\n\nThe **execution** happens through `do_teardown_appcontext` (`app.py:1453`), which is called by `AppContext.pop()` (`ctx.py:496`).\n\n**Complete trigger chain (in order):**\n\n```\n1. HTTP request ends OR CLI command ends OR manual `with app.app_context()` exits\n   ΓåÆ ctx.__exit__(exc_type, exc_val, tb)         ctx.py:510\n   ΓåÆ ctx.pop(exc_val)                            ctx.py:446\n       Γö£ΓöÇΓöÇ do_teardown_request(ctx, exc)          app.py:1420   [if has_request]\n       Γöé   Γö£ΓöÇΓöÇ teardown_request_funcs callbacks   (user registered)\n       Γöé   ΓööΓöÇΓöÇ request_tearing_down.send(...)     signals.py\n       ΓööΓöÇΓöÇ do_teardown_appcontext(ctx, exc)       app.py:1453\n           Γö£ΓöÇΓöÇ reversed(teardown_appcontext_funcs)  [LIFO order]\n           Γöé   ΓööΓöÇΓöÇ ensure_sync(func)(exc)          (user registered via @teardown_appcontext)\n           ΓööΓöÇΓöÇ appcontext_tearing_down.send(...)   signals.py\n\n2. Via wsgi_app `finally` block (app.py:1616):\n   ctx.pop(error)    ΓåÆ same chain as above\n\n3. Via Flask CLI (cli.py):\n   AppContext is pushed for each CLI command; popped after ΓåÆ same chain\n```\n\n**Registration point:** `@app.teardown_appcontext` calls `teardown_appcontext(f)` at `sansio/app.py:827`, which appends `f` to `teardown_appcontext_funcs`. Execution always runs in **LIFO** (reversed) order.\n\n**Signal emitted after all teardown functions:** `appcontext_tearing_down` from `signals.py`.\n\n---\n\n## Q33. Files Affected If `Blueprint` Class Changes ΓÇö Dependency Chain Depth\n\n`Blueprint` is defined in two places (sansio layer + WSGI layer):\n- `src/flask/sansio/blueprints.py` (pure sansio `SansioBlueprint`)\n- `src/flask/blueprints.py:18` (`Blueprint(SansioBlueprint)` ΓÇö adds CLI and file-serving)\n\n**Hop 1 ΓÇö direct importers of `blueprints.py`:**\n\n| File | Import |\n|---|---|\n| `src/flask/__init__.py:3` | `from .blueprints import Blueprint as Blueprint` |\n| `src/flask/debughelpers.py:8` | `from .blueprints import Blueprint` |\n\n**Hop 1 ΓÇö direct importers of `sansio/blueprints.py`:**\n\n| File | Import |\n|---|---|\n| `src/flask/blueprints.py:10` | `from .sansio.blueprints import Blueprint as SansioBlueprint` |\n| `src/flask/sansio/app.py:41` | TYPE_CHECKING `from .blueprints import Blueprint` |\n\n**Hop 2 ΓÇö via `__init__.py` or `sansio/app.py`:**\n- Everything that does `from flask import Blueprint` (all user code and test files)\n- `src/flask/app.py` ΓÇö inherits `App` which has `register_blueprint`, `iter_blueprints`, template loader iterating blueprints\n- `src/flask/templating.py` ΓÇö `DispatchingJinjaLoader._iter_loaders` iterates `app.iter_blueprints()`\n\n**What would break:**\n1. **`SansioBlueprint` changes** ΓÇö `BlueprintSetupState`, all `register_blueprint` logic in `sansio/app.py`, all `deferred_functions` execution.\n2. **`Blueprint.__init__` (WSGI layer)** ΓÇö `.cli` attribute, `AppGroup`, CLI command registration.\n3. **`send_static_file` / `get_send_file_max_age`** ΓÇö static file serving for blueprints.\n4. **`blueprints` attribute on requests** ΓÇö `ctx.request.blueprints` is used in `preprocess_request`, `process_response`, `do_teardown_request`, `_find_error_handler`.\n\n**Dependency chain depth: 2 hops** to all application-level code; the sansio/WSGI split means changes to `SansioBlueprint` ripple upward.\n\n---\n\n## Q34. What Calls `handle_exception` ΓÇö Full Error Propagation Chain\n\n`handle_exception` is defined at `src/flask/app.py:897`. This is the absolute entry point. Its only job is to delegate to `wsgi_app`.\n\n```python\ndef __call__(self, environ, start_response):\n    return self.wsgi_app(environ, start_response)\n```\n\n### Phase 2: Context Setup and Teardown Shell\n\n**`Flask.wsgi_app`** (`src/flask/app.py:1566`) ΓÇö Wraps the entire request in a try/finally that guarantees `ctx.pop()` is always called.\n\n1. **`Flask.request_context`** (`src/flask/app.py:1501`) ΓÇö Calls `AppContext.from_environ(self, environ)`, constructing a new `AppContext` containing the `Request` object parsed from the WSGI environ.\n2. **`AppContext.from_environ`** (`src/flask/ctx.py:340`) ΓÇö Creates the `Request` via `app.request_class(environ)`, attaches `app.json`, returns `AppContext(app, request=request)`.\n3. **`AppContext.__init__`** (`src/flask/ctx.py:300`) ΓÇö Initialises `.g`, `.url_adapter`, `._request`, `._session=None`, `._cv_token=None`. On any exception, calls `handle_user_exception`.\n9. **`Flask.preprocess_request`** (`src/flask/app.py:1363`) ΓÇö Iterates `url_value_preprocessors` then `before_request_funcs` (app-level `None` key, then blueprint keys). Stops and returns a value if any `before_request` handler returns non-None.\n10. **`Flask.dispatch_request`** (`src/flask/app.py:966`) ΓÇö Reads `ctx.request.url_rule.endpoint`, looks up `self.view_functions[endpoint]`, wraps it in `ensure_sync`, and calls it with `**view_args`.\n11. **`Flask.ensure_sync`** (`src/flask/app.py:1065`) ΓÇö Returns `async_to_sync(func)` for coroutine functions (via `asgiref`), or returns sync functions unchanged.\n\n### Phase 4: Response Finalization\n\n12. **`Flask.finalize_request`** (`src/flask/app.py:1021`) ΓÇö Calls `make_response(rv)`, then `process_response(ctx, response)`, then fires `request_finished` signal.\n13. **`Flask.make_response`** (`src/flask/app.py:1224`) ΓÇö Normalises the view return value (string, bytes, dict, tuple, `Response`) into a `Response` instance.\n14. **`Flask.process_response`** (`src/flask/app.py:1394`) ΓÇö Calls per-request `_after_request_functions`, then registered `after_request_funcs` (blueprint order reversed, then app-level), then calls `session_interface.save_session(app, session, response)` to write the `Set-Cookie` header.\n\n### Phase 5: Teardown (always runs in `finally`)\n\n15. **`ctx.pop(error)`** (`src/flask/ctx.py:446`) ΓÇö Calls `app.do_teardown_request(ctx, exc)`, `request.close()`, `app.do_teardown_appcontext(ctx, exc)`, then `_cv_app.reset(token)`.\n16. **`Flask.do_teardown_request`** (`src/flask/app.py:1420`) ΓÇö Runs all `teardown_request_funcs`, fires `request_tearing_down` signal.\n17. **`Flask.do_teardown_appcontext`** (`src/flask/app.py:1453`) ΓÇö Runs all `teardown_appcontext_funcs`, fires `appcontext_tearing_down` signal.\n\n### Exception sub-path\n\nIf an exception escapes `full_dispatch_request`, `wsgi_app` catches it:\n\n- **`Flask.handle_exception`** (`src/flask/app.py:897`) ΓÇö Fires `got_request_exception` signal. If `PROPAGATE_EXCEPTIONS` is True re-raises; otherwise wraps in `InternalServerError`, finds a 500 handler via `_find_error_handler`, then calls `finalize_request(..., from_error_handler=True)`.\n- **`Flask.handle_user_exception`** (`src/flask/app.py:865`) ΓÇö Called from within `full_dispatch_request`. For `HTTPException` subclasses, delegates to `handle_http_exception`. For others, searches `_find_error_handler` directly; re-raises if no handler.\n- **`Flask.handle_http_exception`** (`src/flask/app.py:830`) ΓÇö Skips `RoutingException` types (internal use); calls `_find_error_handler(e, blueprints)`.\n\nThe final response object is then iterated by `response(environ, start_response)` at `app.py:1604` to feed bytes back to the WSGI server.\n\n---\n\n## Q15. Application Context vs Request Context ΓÇö Lifecycle and Access Rules\n\n### Flask 3.x Unified Model\n\nIn Flask 3.x (specifically 3.2+), there is a **single class `AppContext`** (`src/flask/ctx.py:260`) that represents both concepts. The old `RequestContext` is now an alias for `AppContext` and will be removed in Flask 4.0. The distinction is tracked by the boolean property `has_request` (`ctx.py:351`), which is `True` when the context was constructed with a `request` argument.\n\n### AppContext (App Context)\n\nPushed for every request **and** every CLI command. Provides:\n- `current_app` ΓÇö the Flask application instance\n- `g` ΓÇö per-context scratch space (`_AppCtxGlobals`, `ctx.py:30`)\n\n**Pushed:** `ctx.push()` (`ctx.py:416`) is called in `wsgi_app` before dispatch (`app.py:1596`), or when you enter `with app.app_context()`.\n\n**Popped:** `ctx.pop()` (`ctx.py:446`) is called in the `finally` block of `wsgi_app` (`app.py:1616`), or on exit from the `with` block.\n\nInside `push()`:\n```python\nself._cv_token = _cv_app.set(self)   # ctx.py:433\nappcontext_pushed.send(self.app)     # ctx.py:434\n```\n\nInside `pop()`:\n```python\napp.do_teardown_request(ctx, exc)    # ctx.py:490\napp.do_teardown_appcontext(ctx, exc) # ctx.py:496\n_cv_app.reset(self._cv_token)        # ctx.py:498\n```\n\n### Request Context\n\nThe same `AppContext` object, but constructed via `AppContext.from_environ(app, environ)` (`ctx.py:340`), so `._request` is not `None` and `has_request` returns `True`. This is created by `Flask.request_context(environ)` (`app.py:1501`) and by `Flask.test_request_context(...)` (`app.py:1517`).\n\nWhen `has_request` is True, the context additionally provides:\n- `request` ΓÇö the `Request` object\n- `session` ΓÇö the deserialized session (lazy-loaded on first access via `_get_session()`, `ctx.py:381`)\n- URL matching via `match_request()` (`ctx.py:405`)\n\n### What Happens Outside a Context\n\n`request` is defined as:\n```python\n# src/flask/globals.py:57-59\nrequest: RequestProxy = LocalProxy(\n    _cv_app, \"request\", unbound_message=_no_req_msg\n)\n```\n\nIf `_cv_app.get()` returns nothing (no context pushed), `LocalProxy` raises a `RuntimeError` with the message:\n\n```\nWorking outside of request context.\nAttempted to use functionality that expected an active HTTP request.\n```\n\n`current_app` and `g` raise a `RuntimeError` with:\n```\nWorking outside of application context.\n```\n\nThe error messages are defined in `src/flask/globals.py:33-56`.\n\n---\n\n## Q16. LocalProxy and ContextVar ΓÇö Internal Mechanism\n\n### The Single Source of Truth\n\n```python\n# src/flask/globals.py:40\n_cv_app: ContextVar[AppContext] = ContextVar(\"flask.app_ctx\")\n```\n\nThis is a `contextvars.ContextVar` from Python's stdlib. Each OS thread ΓÇö and each `asyncio` Task ΓÇö has an independent slot in the `ContextVar`. Two concurrent requests in two threads each see a completely different `AppContext` value for the same `_cv_app` variable.\n\n### Proxy Definitions\n\n```python\n# src/flask/globals.py:41-62\napp_ctx: AppContextProxy = LocalProxy(_cv_app, unbound_message=_no_app_msg)\ncurrent_app: FlaskProxy = LocalProxy(_cv_app, \"app\", unbound_message=_no_app_msg)\ng: _AppCtxGlobalsProxy = LocalProxy(_cv_app, \"g\", unbound_message=_no_app_msg)\nrequest: RequestProxy = LocalProxy(_cv_app, \"request\", unbound_message=_no_req_msg)\nsession: SessionMixinProxy = LocalProxy(_cv_app, \"session\", unbound_message=_no_req_msg)\n```\n\n`LocalProxy` is a Werkzeug class (`werkzeug.local.LocalProxy`). When passed a `ContextVar` as its first argument, it resolves on every attribute access by:\n1. Calling `_cv_app.get()` to retrieve the current thread's `AppContext`\n2. Optionally accessing an attribute on the result (e.g., `\"app\"`, `\"g\"`, `\"request\"`, `\"session\"`)\n3. Forwarding the subsequent attribute access or method call to that resolved object\n\n### Resolution is Deferred\n\n```python\nfrom flask import request    # no resolution ΓÇö import is cheap\nrequest.method               # resolution happens HERE: _cv_app.get().request.method\n```\n\nThis is why importing `request` at module level is safe even before any request has started ΓÇö the import just names the proxy object.\n\n### Push and Pop via ContextVar Tokens\n\n`ctx.push()` (`ctx.py:433`):\n```python\nself._cv_token = _cv_app.set(self)\n```\n`ctx.pop()` (`ctx.py:498`):\n```python\n_cv_app.reset(self._cv_token)\n```\n\nThe token returned by `ContextVar.set()` records the previous value. `reset(token)` restores exactly that prior value, making contexts safely nestable (useful in tests and CLI).\n\n### Thread Safety\n\nEach OS thread has its own `contextvars.Context` copy. The `ContextVar` specification (PEP 567) guarantees isolation without locks. For async code, each `asyncio.Task` also inherits a copy of the context at creation time, so a task pushed via `copy_current_request_context` (`ctx.py:154`) runs in an isolated copy of the current `AppContext`.\n\n### `_AppCtxGlobals` ΓÇö `g`\n\n`g` is an instance of `_AppCtxGlobals` (`ctx.py:30`), a plain namespace object that stores arbitrary attributes in `__dict__`. It is created fresh for every `AppContext.__init__` call (`ctx.py:312`), so it lives for exactly one request lifetime.\n\n---\n\n## Q17. Blueprint Registration ΓÇö Internal Steps\n\n### Triggering Registration\n\n`app.register_blueprint(blueprint, **options)` is defined at `src/flask/sansio/app.py:570`. Its sole action is:\n```python\nblueprint.register(self, options)   # sansio/app.py:595\n```\n\n### `Blueprint.register` (`src/flask/sansio/blueprints.py:273`)\n\nThis is the real worker. Steps in order:\n\n1. **Name collision check** (`bp.py:306-314`) ΓÇö Builds the fully-qualified name (`name_prefix.self_name`). If that name is already in `app.blueprints` pointing to a different object, raises `ValueError`.\n\n2. **Register in `app.blueprints`** (`bp.py:319`) ΓÇö `app.blueprints[name] = self`. Marks `self._got_registered_once = True`, which makes any future `@blueprint.route()` decorator raise `AssertionError` (setup must happen before registration).\n\n3. **Create `BlueprintSetupState`** (`bp.py:321`) ΓÇö Calls `self.make_setup_state(app, options, first_bp_registration)`. `BlueprintSetupState.__init__` (`bp.py:41`) resolves the final `url_prefix`, `subdomain`, `name_prefix`, and `url_defaults` by merging blueprint defaults with override options.\n\n4. **Static route** (`bp.py:323-328`) ΓÇö If the blueprint has a `static_folder`, immediately calls `state.add_url_rule(...)` for the static file route. `BlueprintSetupState.add_url_rule` (`bp.py:87`) prepends the URL prefix and namespace-qualifies the endpoint name as `name_prefix.name.endpoint`, then delegates to `app.add_url_rule(...)`.\n\n5. **`_merge_blueprint_funcs`** (`bp.py:379-410`) ΓÇö Called only on the first registration (or first use of a given name). Copies all of the blueprint's hook registries into the app's corresponding registries, renaming keys from `None` (blueprint-global) to `<bp_name>` and from `<sub_bp_name>` to `<bp_name>.<sub_bp_name>`:\n   - `error_handler_spec`\n   - `view_functions`\n   - `before_request_funcs`\n   - `after_request_funcs`\n   - `teardown_request_funcs`\n   - `url_default_functions`\n   - `url_value_preprocessors`\n   - `template_context_processors`\n\n6. **Run deferred functions** (`bp.py:334-335`) ΓÇö Iterates `self.deferred_functions` and calls each with `state`. Every `@blueprint.route(...)` decorator called before `register_blueprint` appended a lambda to `deferred_functions` via `Blueprint.add_url_rule` ΓåÆ `Blueprint.record` (`bp.py:224`). Those lambdas now call `state.add_url_rule(...)` which ultimately calls `app.add_url_rule(rule, endpoint, view_func)`.\n\n7. **CLI registration** (`bp.py:337-347`) ΓÇö Merges or adds the blueprint's Click command group to `app.cli` based on `cli_group` setting.\n\n8. **Recurse into nested blueprints** (`bp.py:349-377`) ΓÇö For each `(child_bp, child_options)` in `self._blueprints`, resolves combined subdomain and URL prefix, sets `name_prefix` to the current name, then calls `child_bp.register(app, bp_options)` recursively.\n\n### `app.add_url_rule` (`src/flask/sansio/app.py:604`)\n\nCreates a `werkzeug.routing.Rule(rule, methods=methods, **options)` and calls `self.url_map.add(rule_obj)`. The view function is stored in `self.view_functions[endpoint]`. This is where `werkzeug.routing.Map` gains knowledge of the route.\n\n---\n\n## Q18. Error Handling Hierarchy\n\n### The Three Entry Points\n\n- **`handle_user_exception(ctx, e)`** (`app.py:865`) ΓÇö called inside `full_dispatch_request` for any exception that escapes the view or `before_request` hooks.\n- **`handle_exception(ctx, e)`** (`app.py:897`) ΓÇö called from `wsgi_app`'s outer except block for exceptions that escape `full_dispatch_request` itself (including exceptions from error handlers).\n- **`handle_http_exception(ctx, e)`** (`app.py:830`) ΓÇö called by `handle_user_exception` for `HTTPException` instances.\n\n### Exact Order in `handle_user_exception` (`app.py:865`)\n\n1. **`BadRequestKeyError` special case** (`app.py:882`) ΓÇö If the exception is a `BadRequestKeyError` and `debug=True` or `TRAP_BAD_REQUEST_ERRORS=True`, sets `e.show_exception = True` to expose the bad key name in the response.\n2. **`trap_http_exception` check** (`app.py:887`) ΓÇö If `TRAP_HTTP_EXCEPTIONS=True`, the exception is re-raised rather than handled (lets debugger see it). `trap_http_exception` is also True for `InternalServerError` when in debug mode.\n3. **Delegate `HTTPException` to `handle_http_exception`** (`app.py:888`).\n4. **Search for a non-HTTP exception handler** (`app.py:890`) ΓÇö Calls `_find_error_handler(e, ctx.request.blueprints)`.\n5. **If no handler found**, the exception is re-raised (`app.py:893`).\n6. **If a handler is found**, it is wrapped in `ensure_sync` and called (`app.py:895`).\n\n### Exact Order in `handle_http_exception` (`app.py:830`)\n\n1. **Proxy exception check** (`app.py:851`) ΓÇö If `e.code is None` (proxy exception), returns `e` unchanged.\n2. **`RoutingException` check** (`app.py:857`) ΓÇö If it is a `RoutingException` (used internally for slash redirects), returns it unchanged.\n3. **`_find_error_handler` lookup** (`app.py:860`).\n4. **If no handler**, returns `e` (the HTTPException becomes the response directly).\n5. **If handler found**, calls it.\n\n### `_find_error_handler` Lookup Order (`sansio/app.py:868`)\n\n```python\nfor c in (code, None) if code is not None else (None,):\n    for name in names:   # names = (*blueprints, None)\n        handler_map = self.error_handler_spec[name][c]\n        for cls in exc_class.__mro__:\n            handler = handler_map.get(cls)\n            if handler is not None:\n                return handler\n```\n\nPriority order (highest to lowest):\n1. **Blueprint-specific handler for this exact HTTP code** (innermost blueprint first, outermost last)\n2. **App-level handler for this exact HTTP code**\n3. **Blueprint-specific handler matching a class in the exception's MRO** (without code filter)\n4. **App-level handler matching a class in the exception's MRO**\n5. **None** ΓÇö no match\n\nThe MRO walk means a handler registered for `HTTPException` catches all HTTP exceptions if no more specific handler exists.\n\n### Unhandled 500 path in `handle_exception` (`app.py:897`)\n\n1. Fires `got_request_exception` signal (`app.py:926`).\n2. Checks `PROPAGATE_EXCEPTIONS` (auto-True when `TESTING` or `DEBUG`). If True, re-raises.\n3. Logs via `log_exception` (`app.py:940`).\n4. Wraps in `InternalServerError(original_exception=e)`.\n5. Calls `_find_error_handler(server_error, ...)` ΓÇö any handler for 500 or `InternalServerError`.\n6. Calls `finalize_request(..., from_error_handler=True)` which suppresses further exceptions.\n\n---\n\n## Q19. Session Lifecycle ΓÇö Cookie to Object and Back\n\n### Inbound: Cookie to Session Object\n\n**Step 1 ΓÇö `ctx.push()`** (`ctx.py:436-439`) ΓÇö When a request context is pushed, `_get_session()` is called immediately:\n\n```python\nif self._request is not None:\n    self._get_session()\n    if self.url_adapter is not None:\n        self.match_request()\n```\n\n**Step 2 ΓÇö `AppContext._get_session()`** (`ctx.py:381`) ΓÇö Calls `app.session_interface.open_session(app, self.request)`. For the default interface this is `SecureCookieSessionInterface.open_session`.\n\n**Step 3 ΓÇö `SecureCookieSessionInterface.open_session`** (`sessions.py:323`):\n1. Calls `self.get_signing_serializer(app)` ΓåÆ builds a `URLSafeTimedSerializer` (from `itsdangerous`) using `app.secret_key` plus any `SECRET_KEY_FALLBACKS`, with `salt=\"cookie-session\"` and `digest_method=sha1` and `key_derivation=\"hmac\"`.\n2. Reads `request.cookies.get(SESSION_COOKIE_NAME)` (default name `\"session\"`).\n3. If no cookie, returns an empty `SecureCookieSession()`.\n4. If cookie present, calls `s.loads(val, max_age=int(permanent_session_lifetime.total_seconds()))`. This verifies the HMAC signature and checks the timestamp. On `BadSignature`, returns an empty session.\n5. The session data was serialised by `TaggedJSONSerializer` (`sessions.py:273`, `json/tag.py`), which extends JSON with tags for Python types like `datetime`, `tuple`, `bytes`. `loads` deserialises it back.\n6. Returns `SecureCookieSession(data)` ΓÇö a `CallbackDict` that sets `.modified = True` on any mutation.\n\n**Step 4 ΓÇö `ctx.session` property** (`ctx.py:396`) ΓÇö Sets `session.accessed = True`, triggering `Vary: Cookie` header logic later.\n\n**Step 5 ΓÇö In the view** ΓÇö `session` proxy (`globals.py:60`) resolves to `_cv_app.get().session` ΓåÆ the `SecureCookieSession` dict.\n\n### Outbound: Session Object to Set-Cookie Header\n\n**Step 1 ΓÇö `Flask.process_response`** (`app.py:1415`):\n```python\nif not self.session_interface.is_null_session(ctx._get_session()):\n    self.session_interface.save_session(self, ctx._get_session(), response)\n```\n\n**Step 2 ΓÇö `SecureCookieSessionInterface.save_session`** (`sessions.py:337`):\n1. Reads all cookie parameters from config: `name`, `domain`, `path`, `secure`, `partitioned`, `samesite`, `httponly`.\n2. If `session.accessed`, adds `Vary: Cookie` to response headers (`sessions.py:350`).\n3. If session is empty and modified (was deleted): calls `response.delete_cookie(name, ...)` (`sessions.py:356`).\n4. If session is empty and not modified: returns without writing a cookie.\n5. Calls `should_set_cookie(app, session)` (`sessions.py:233`): returns `True` if `session.modified` OR (`session.permanent` AND `SESSION_REFRESH_EACH_REQUEST=True`).\n6. Computes expiry via `get_expiration_time` ΓÇö returns `now + PERMANENT_SESSION_LIFETIME` if `session.permanent`, else `None` (browser session cookie).\n7. Serialises with `self.get_signing_serializer(app).dumps(dict(session))` ΓÇö `TaggedJSONSerializer` serialises to JSON, `URLSafeTimedSerializer` signs with HMAC and base64-encodes.\n8. Calls `response.set_cookie(name, val, expires=..., httponly=..., ...)` ΓåÆ adds `Set-Cookie` header.\n\n---\n\n## Q20. Signal System\n\n### Library\n\nFlask uses **blinker** (`src/flask/signals.py:3`). All signals are created in a private `blinker.Namespace` called `_signals` to avoid name collisions with user-defined signals.\n\n### All Defined Signals (`src/flask/signals.py`)\n\n```python\ntemplate_rendered        = _signals.signal(\"template-rendered\")        # line 8\nbefore_render_template   = _signals.signal(\"before-render-template\")   # line 9\nrequest_started          = _signals.signal(\"request-started\")          # line 10\nrequest_finished         = _signals.signal(\"request-finished\")         # line 11\nrequest_tearing_down     = _signals.signal(\"request-tearing-down\")     # line 12\ngot_request_exception    = _signals.signal(\"got-request-exception\")    # line 13\nappcontext_tearing_down  = _signals.signal(\"appcontext-tearing-down\")  # line 14\nappcontext_pushed        = _signals.signal(\"appcontext-pushed\")        # line 15\nappcontext_popped        = _signals.signal(\"appcontext-popped\")        # line 16\nmessage_flashed          = _signals.signal(\"message-flashed\")          # line 17\n```\n\n### Exact Firing Points\n\n| Signal | Fired in | File:Line | Extra kwargs |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `appcontext_pushed` | `AppContext.push` | `ctx.py:434` | ΓÇö |\n| `request_started` | `Flask.full_dispatch_request` | `app.py:1013` | ΓÇö |\n| `request_finished` | `Flask.finalize_request` | `app.py:1042` | `response` |\n| `got_request_exception` | `Flask.handle_exception` | `app.py:926` | `exception` |\n| `request_tearing_down` | `Flask.do_teardown_request` | `app.py:1449` | `exc` |\n| `appcontext_tearing_down` | `Flask.do_teardown_appcontext` | `app.py:1477` | `exc` |\n| `appcontext_popped` | `AppContext.pop` (after reset) | `ctx.py:499` ΓÇö see below | `exc` |\n| `before_render_template` | `templating._render` | `templating.py:126` | `template`, `context` |\n| `template_rendered` | `templating._render` | `templating.py:130` | `template`, `context` |\n| `message_flashed` | `helpers.flash` | `helpers.py` | `message`, `category` |\n\nNote: `appcontext_popped` is sent after `_cv_app.reset(token)`, with `sender=app` and `exc=exc`. The `_async_wrapper=app.ensure_sync` argument on every `.send()` call means signal receivers that are `async def` functions can be automatically wrapped if needed.\n\n### Subscribing\n\n```python\nfrom flask import request_finished\n\n@request_finished.connect_via(app)\ndef log_response(sender, response, **extra):\n    print(response.status_code)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Q21. Template Context ΓÇö Automatic Variables\n\n### `create_jinja_environment` (`src/flask/app.py:469`)\n\nWhen `Flask.jinja_env` is accessed for the first time (lazy `cached_property` at `sansio/app.py:466`), `create_jinja_environment` is called. It injects these **global** Jinja variables, always present in every template regardless of context:\n\n```python\nrv.globals.update(\n    url_for=self.url_for,\n    get_flashed_messages=get_flashed_messages,\n    config=self.config,\n    request=request,       # the LocalProxy\n    session=session,       # the LocalProxy\n    g=g,                   # the LocalProxy\n)\n```\n(`src/flask/app.py:495-505`)\n\nThese are the proxy objects ΓÇö they work in all templates including those imported via `{% import %}`.\n\n### `_default_template_ctx_processor` (`src/flask/templating.py:21`)\n\nRegistered by `Scaffold.__init__` in `template_context_processors[None]`. For each template render, `update_template_context` calls it and it returns:\n\n```python\n{\"g\": ctx.g}                         # always\n{\"request\": ctx.request}             # only if has_request\n```\n\nThis replaces the proxy objects with the actual concrete objects in the render context for performance. The `session` proxy is intentionally not replaced here because accessing the concrete session object triggers `session.accessed = True` which must happen at the right time (comment at `templating.py:31`).\n\n### `update_template_context` (`src/flask/app.py:590`)\n\nCalled from `templating._render` (`templating.py:125`). It:\n\n1. Builds the list of `names` to check: `(None, *reversed(request.blueprints))` ΓÇö app-level processors first, then blueprint processors from outermost to innermost.\n2. For each name with registered context processors, calls each processor and merges the result.\n3. Reapplies `orig_ctx` (the caller-supplied variables) last, so explicit render-time variables always win over context processors.\n\n### Complete list of auto-available variables in every template\n\n| Variable | Source | Notes |\n|---|---|---|\n| `request` | `jinja_env.globals` + `_default_template_ctx_processor` | The current request object |\n| `session` | `jinja_env.globals` (proxy only) | The current session dict |\n| `g` | `jinja_env.globals` + `_default_template_ctx_processor` | Per-request scratch space |\n| `config` | `jinja_env.globals` | The app's `Config` dict |\n| `url_for` | `jinja_env.globals` | URL building function |\n| `get_flashed_messages` | `jinja_env.globals` | Returns flash messages |\n\n---\n\n## Q22. Configuration Loading ΓÇö Priority and Merging\n\n### `Config` Class (`src/flask/config.py:50`)\n\n`Config` is a plain `dict` subclass. It accepts only **uppercase keys** (enforced in `from_object`, `from_mapping`). There is no built-in priority mechanism ΓÇö each load call simply overwrites existing keys with new values. The last write wins.\n\n### Default Values\n\nSet in `Flask.default_config` (`app.py:206`) ΓÇö an `ImmutableDict` with defaults for all 26 built-in keys. Passed to `Config.__init__` as `defaults`. These are always loaded first.\n\n### Loading Methods (each described with what it does internally)\n\n**`from_object(obj)`** (`config.py:218`) ΓÇö Accepts a string import path or an object. Calls `dir(obj)` and sets every uppercase attribute:\n```python\nfor key in dir(obj):\n    if key.isupper():\n        self[key] = getattr(obj, key)\n```\n\n**`from_pyfile(filename)`** (`config.py:187`) ΓÇö Reads a `.cfg` (or any `.py`) file, compiles it into a temporary `types.ModuleType`, execs it, then calls `self.from_object(d)`. Paths are relative to `app.root_path` (or `instance_path` if `instance_relative_config=True`).\n\n**`from_envvar(variable_name)`** (`config.py:102`) ΓÇö Reads `os.environ[variable_name]` to get a file path, then calls `self.from_pyfile(rv)`. It is literally a shortcut for `from_pyfile(os.environ['VAR'])`.\n\n**`from_prefixed_env(prefix='FLASK')`** (`config.py:126`) ΓÇö Scans `os.environ` for keys starting with `FLASK_`, strips the prefix, attempts `json.loads` on the value (to handle booleans, ints, dicts), then sets the key. Double-underscore `__` in a key creates nested dict access.\n\n**`from_file(filename, load)`** (`config.py:256`) ΓÇö Generic: opens a file, calls `load(f)` (any callable: `json.load`, `tomllib.load`, etc.), passes the result to `from_mapping`.\n\n**`from_mapping(mapping, **kwargs)`** (`config.py:304`) ΓÇö Sets all uppercase keys from the mapping. Base primitive used by `from_file`.\n\n### Priority Order\n\nThere is no automatic merging or override system ΓÇö each method unconditionally writes over existing keys. The de-facto priority is determined entirely by the **order you call them**. A common pattern:\n\n```python\napp.config.from_object(\"yourapp.default_config\")  # 1. lowest priority defaults\napp.config.from_pyfile(\"config.cfg\", silent=True)  # 2. deployment config\napp.config.from_envvar(\"YOURAPP_SETTINGS\", silent=True)  # 3. env-specified override\napp.config.from_prefixed_env()  # 4. highest priority: FLASK_* env vars\n```\n\nThe **last call wins** for any given key. There is no atomic merge ΓÇö values are replaced one key at a time.\n\n---\n\n## Q23. Session Cookie Config Keys\n\nAll defaults are defined in `Flask.default_config` at `src/flask/app.py:206`. The `SessionInterface` accessor methods live in `src/flask/sessions.py`.\n\n| Key | Type | Default | What It Controls |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `SESSION_COOKIE_NAME` | `str` | `\"session\"` | The name of the cookie as it appears in the `Cookie:` and `Set-Cookie:` headers |\n| `SESSION_COOKIE_DOMAIN` | `str \\| None` | `None` | The `Domain` attribute. `None` means the cookie is sent only to the exact domain that set it (no subdomains). Set to `\"example.com\"` to cover subdomains |\n| `SESSION_COOKIE_PATH` | `str \\| None` | `None` | The `Path` attribute. `None` falls back to `APPLICATION_ROOT` (default `\"/\"`) |\n| `SESSION_COOKIE_HTTPONLY` | `bool` | `True` | Sets the `HttpOnly` flag. Blocks JavaScript `document.cookie` access |\n| `SESSION_COOKIE_SECURE` | `bool` | `False` | Sets the `Secure` flag. Browser will only send the cookie over HTTPS |\n| `SESSION_COOKIE_SAMESITE` | `str \\| None` | `None` | Sets the `SameSite` attribute. Valid values: `\"Strict\"`, `\"Lax\"`, `\"None\"`. CSRF mitigation |\n| `SESSION_COOKIE_PARTITIONED` | `bool` | `False` | Sets the `Partitioned` flag (CHIPS ΓÇö Cookies Having Independent Partitioned State). For Chrome's privacy sandbox |\n| `SESSION_REFRESH_EACH_REQUEST` | `bool` | `True` | If `True` and session is permanent, resets the cookie expiry on every request even if the session was not modified |\n| `PERMANENT_SESSION_LIFETIME` | `timedelta \\| int` | `timedelta(days=31)` | The maximum age of a permanent session cookie. Integers are treated as seconds. Accessed via `app.permanent_session_lifetime` |\n| `SECRET_KEY` | `str \\| bytes \\| None` | `None` | Required for signing. If `None`, `get_signing_serializer` returns `None` and `open_session` returns `None`, causing a `NullSession` to be created |\n| `SECRET_KEY_FALLBACKS` | `list \\| None` | `None` | List of old keys still valid for signature verification during key rotation. The current key is always used for signing |\n\nAccessor methods (`sessions.py`):\n- `get_cookie_name` at `sessions.py:171`\n- `get_cookie_domain` at `sessions.py:175`\n- `get_cookie_path` at `sessions.py:187`\n- `get_cookie_httponly` at `sessions.py:195`\n- `get_cookie_secure` at `sessions.py:202`\n- `get_cookie_samesite` at `sessions.py:208`\n- `get_cookie_partitioned` at `sessions.py:215`\n- `get_expiration_time` at `sessions.py:223`\n- `should_set_cookie` at `sessions.py:233`\n\n---\n\n## Q24. URL Routing Internals\n\n### Registration Phase\n\n1. **`@app.route(\"/path\")`** calls `Scaffold.route` (defined in `src/flask/sansio/scaffold.py`) which calls `self.add_url_rule(rule, endpoint, view_func, **options)`.\n\n2. **`App.add_url_rule`** (`sansio/app.py:604`):\n   - Infers endpoint name from view function name if not given.\n   - Resolves `methods` set (defaults to `{\"GET\"}`); adds `\"OPTIONS\"` if `PROVIDE_AUTOMATIC_OPTIONS=True`.\n   - Creates `self.url_rule_class(rule, methods=methods, **options)` ΓÇö a `werkzeug.routing.Rule` object.\n   - Calls `self.url_map.add(rule_obj)` to register the `Rule` in the `werkzeug.routing.Map`.\n   - Stores `view_func` in `self.view_functions[endpoint]`.\n\n### The URL Map\n\n`self.url_map` is a `werkzeug.routing.Map` instance, created in `App.__init__` at `sansio/app.py:402`:\n```python\nself.url_map = self.url_map_class(host_matching=host_matching)\n```\n\n`werkzeug.routing.Map` compiles all `Rule` objects into an internal regex-based matching automaton.\n\n### Request Time: URL Matching\n\n3. **`AppContext.__init__`** (`ctx.py:326`) calls `app.create_url_adapter(request)`.\n\n4. **`Flask.create_url_adapter`** (`app.py:509`) calls `url_map.bind_to_environ(request.environ, server_name=..., subdomain=...)`, returning a `werkzeug.routing.MapAdapter` bound to the current host, scheme, and script root.\n\n5. **`AppContext.push()`** (`ctx.py:443`) calls `self.match_request()`.\n\n6. **`AppContext.match_request()`** (`ctx.py:405`):\n   ```python\n   result = self.url_adapter.match(return_rule=True)\n   self._request.url_rule, self._request.view_args = result\n   ```\n   `MapAdapter.match()` walks the compiled routing table. On a match, it returns `(Rule, view_args_dict)`. On no match it raises `werkzeug.exceptions.NotFound`; on wrong method it raises `werkzeug.exceptions.MethodNotAllowed`. These exceptions are caught and stored in `request.routing_exception`.\n\n7. **`Flask.dispatch_request`** (`app.py:966`):\n   - Checks `req.routing_exception` ΓÇö if set, calls `self.raise_routing_exception(req)` which re-raises the stored exception.\n   - Looks up `self.view_functions[rule.endpoint]`.\n   - Calls `self.ensure_sync(view_functions[endpoint])(**view_args)`.\n\n### URL Building (`url_for`)\n\n**`Flask.url_for`** (`app.py:1102`) / **`helpers.url_for`** (calls `current_app.url_for`):\n1. Gets `url_adapter` from `ctx.url_adapter` (in a request) or creates one from `SERVER_NAME` (outside a request).\n2. Calls `self.inject_url_defaults(endpoint, values)` to apply registered `@app.url_defaults` functions.\n3. Calls `url_adapter.build(endpoint, values, method=..., url_scheme=..., force_external=...)`.\n4. On `BuildError`, calls `self.handle_url_build_error(error, endpoint, values)` which tries registered `url_build_error_handlers`.\n\n---\n\n## Q25. Test Client ΓÇö What It Mocks and What It Runs\n\n### `FlaskClient` (`src/flask/testing.py:109`)\n\nInherits from `werkzeug.test.Client`. The Werkzeug `Client` is itself not a mock ΓÇö it calls the real WSGI application callable directly in-process, without any network I/O.\n\n### What `FlaskClient` does NOT mock\n\nEverything in the request pipeline runs for real:\n- `Flask.wsgi_app` (`app.py:1566`) ΓÇö the full WSGI entry point\n- `AppContext.from_environ` and `ctx.push()` ΓÇö full context setup including URL matching and session loading\n- `Flask.full_dispatch_request` ΓÇö `before_request`, `dispatch_request`, `after_request`\n- `Flask.finalize_request` and `process_response` ΓÇö full response finalisation\n- `session_interface.open_session` / `save_session` ΓÇö real session cookie signing via `itsdangerous`\n- `ctx.pop()` and teardown functions\n- All signals\n\n### What `FlaskClient` does add/override\n\n1. **`EnvironBuilder`** (`testing.py:27`) ΓÇö Subclasses `werkzeug.test.EnvironBuilder`. Builds the WSGI environ from test parameters. Reads `app.config[\"SERVER_NAME\"]`, `APPLICATION_ROOT`, and `PREFERRED_URL_SCHEME` to construct the base URL. Uses `app.json.dumps` for JSON serialisation.\n\n2. **`environ_base`** (`testing.py:130`) ΓÇö Injects default WSGI environ values: `REMOTE_ADDR=\"127.0.0.1\"` and `HTTP_USER_AGENT=\"Werkzeug/x.y.z\"`.\n\n3. **`preserve_context`** (`testing.py:127`) ΓÇö When `FlaskClient` is used as a context manager (`with app.test_client() as c:`), sets `preserve_context = True`. This injects a `werkzeug.debug.preserve_context` key into the environ (`testing.py:189`). In `wsgi_app` at `app.py:1606`, Flask checks for this key and calls the callback instead of popping the context, keeping the `AppContext` alive until the `with` block exits. This lets tests access `request`, `g`, and `session` after the response has been returned.\n\n4. **`session_transaction()`** (`testing.py:135`) ΓÇö A context manager that manually opens and saves the session around a `test_request_context`. This lets tests modify session data by going through the real `session_interface`, not by directly editing a dict.\n\n5. **`_context_stack`** (`testing.py:129`) ΓÇö An `ExitStack` that manages preserved contexts across redirects: it is closed before each new request (`testing.py:233`) to prevent stale contexts from leaking between requests.\n\n6. **`open()`** (`testing.py:204`) ΓÇö Overrides Werkzeug's `Client.open` to use `FlaskClient.EnvironBuilder`, copy environ defaults, and handle preserved contexts. Delegates to `super().open()` which calls `app.wsgi_app` directly.\n\n### Summary\n\nThe test client is essentially a thin WSGI request builder that bypasses TCP/IP networking. Every line of Flask application code ΓÇö routing, context management, sessions, signals, before/after request hooks, error handlers ΓÇö runs exactly as in production. The only differences are: the network transport (replaced by an in-process call), some injected environ defaults, and optional context preservation for post-response inspection."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"stop_details":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3920,"cache_read_input_tokens":87822,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":3920,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"diagnostics":null,"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_01SDJVYuazREAXJDtUFhzvws","session_id":"ecdaea3d-793d-427b-9869-5acda3cc8550","uuid":"3f1e15d9-5be2-4816-af73-bda184c7622b","request_id":"req_011Cc85C7atj72VrrMdU6toi","subagent_type":"general-purpose","task_description":"Q14-Q25 Conceptual Architectural"}

Where is `LocalProxy` defined? What does it proxy and how does it resolve the underlying object?\n\n**Definition:** `werkzeug/src/werkzeug/local.py`, line 738 (werkzeug 3.1.8). It is **not** in the Flask codebase ΓÇö it is in the Werkzeug package, imported into Flask at `src/flask/globals.py:6`.\n\n**What it proxies:** Flask uses `LocalProxy` to create five module-level proxy objects in `src/flask/globals.py`:\n- `app_ctx` ΓåÆ the active `AppContext`\n- `current_app` ΓåÆ `ctx.app` (the Flask app)\n- `g` ΓåÆ `ctx.g` (per-request global data)\n- `request` ΓåÆ `ctx.request`\n- `session` ΓåÆ `ctx.session`\n\nEach proxy is backed by the `_cv_app` ContextVar with an optional attribute name argument:\n```python\ncurrent_app = LocalProxy(_cv_app, \"app\", unbound_message=...)\nrequest     = LocalProxy(_cv_app, \"request\", unbound_message=...)\nsession     = LocalProxy(_cv_app, \"session\", unbound_message=...)\ng           = LocalProxy(_cv_app, \"g\", unbound_message=...)\n```\n\n**How it resolves the underlying object:**\n\n`LocalProxy.__init__` stores the lookup source in `__wrapped` (in `__slots__`). It creates a `_get_current_object` closure at init time. For a `ContextVar` argument:\n```python\ndef _get_current_object() -> T:\n    try:\n        obj = local.get()       # ContextVar.get() raises LookupError if unset\n    except LookupError:\n        raise RuntimeError(unbound_message) from None\n    return get_name(obj)        # getattr(obj, attr_name) if attr_name provided\n```\nAll attribute/item accesses on the proxy (via `__getattr__`, `__getitem__`, operators, etc.) are forwarded through `_ProxyLookup` descriptors that call `_get_current_object()` at access time, making the proxy transparent. `__wrapped__` returns the original ContextVar for introspection.\n\n---\n\n## Q6.
