Intended to be overridden.\n\n2. **Concrete implementation** ΓÇö `src/flask/sessions.py`, lines 323ΓÇô335, `SecureCookieSessionInterface.open_session()`:\n   - Calls `self.get_signing_serializer(app)` ΓÇö returns `None` if `app.secret_key` is not set.\n   - If serializer is `None`, returns `None` immediately (secret key missing).\n   - If no cookie named `SESSION_COOKIE_NAME` in the request: returns `self.session_class()` ΓÇö an empty `SecureCookieSession`.\n   - If a cookie exists: calls `s.loads(val, max_age=max_age)` to verify the signature and deserialize. Returns `self.session_class(data)` on success, or `self.session_class()` (empty) on `BadSignature`.\n\n**What happens if it returns `None`:** In `AppContext._get_session()` (lines 381ΓÇô393 of `ctx.py`):\n```python\nself._session = si.open_session(self.app, self.request)\nif self._session is None:\n    self._session = si.make_null_session(self.app)\n```\nA null session is created via `make_null_session()`. A null session raises a `RuntimeError` with a helpful message when you try to read or write it (indicating the secret key is not set), rather than silently losing data.\n\n---\n\n## Q7. Where is `save_session` defined? What arguments does it take and what does it write?\n\n**Two definitions:**\n\n1. **Base class stub** ΓÇö `src/flask/sessions.py`, lines 263ΓÇô270, `SessionInterface.save_session(self, app, session, response)`:\n   - Raises `NotImplementedError`.\n\n2. **Concrete implementation** ΓÇö `src/flask/sessions.py`, lines 337ΓÇô385, `SecureCookieSessionInterface.save_session(self, app: Flask, session: SessionMixin, response: Response) -> None`:\n\n**Arguments:** `app` (the Flask application), `session` (the `SessionMixin` instance), `response` (the `Response` object to write the cookie into).\n\n**What it writes / logic flow:**\n\n1. Reads cookie parameters from the app config: `name`, `domain`, `path`, `secure`, `partitioned`, `samesite`, `httponly`.\n2. If `session.accessed` is `True`, adds `Vary: Cookie` to the response headers.\n3. **Empty + modified session** (lines 354ΓÇô367): If the session is empty and modified, calls `response.delete_cookie(name, ...)` to remove the cookie, and adds `Vary: Cookie`.\n4. **Empty + unmodified session**: returns without writing anything.\n5. **`should_set_cookie` check** (line 369): If `SESSION_REFRESH_EACH_REQUEST` is False and the session is not modified, returns without writing.\n6. **Write the cookie** (lines 372ΓÇô385): Calls `get_signing_serializer(app).dumps(dict(session))` to serialize and HMAC-sign the session data, then calls `response.set_cookie(name, val, expires=..., httponly=..., domain=..., path=..., secure=..., partitioned=..., samesite=...)` which writes the `Set-Cookie` header on the response. Adds `Vary: Cookie`.\n\n---\n\n## Q8. Where is `handle_exception` defined? What is the full flow inside it?\n\n**Definition:** `src/flask/app.py`, lines 897ΓÇô948, method of class `Flask`.\n\n**Full flow:**\n\n1. **Capture exc_info** (line 925): `exc_info = sys.exc_info()` ΓÇö captures the active exception's traceback.\n2. **Send `got_request_exception` signal** (line 926): `got_request_exception.send(self, _async_wrapper=self.ensure_sync, exception=e)` ΓÇö always fired regardless of propagation.\n3. **Read `PROPAGATE_EXCEPTIONS`** (line 927): `propagate = self.config[\"PROPAGATE_EXCEPTIONS\"]`.\n4. **Auto-set propagate** (lines 929ΓÇô930): If `propagate is None`, set it to `self.testing or self.debug`.\n5. **Propagate branch** (lines 932ΓÇô938): If `propagate` is True:\n   - If the exception is the currently active one (`exc_info[1] is e`): bare `raise` to preserve traceback.\n   - Otherwise: `raise e`.\n6. **Log the exception** (line 940): `self.log_exception(ctx, exc_info)` ΓÇö logs at `ERROR` level via `app.logger`.\n7. **Wrap as `InternalServerError`** (line 942): `server_error = InternalServerError(original_exception=e)` ΓÇö always 500, with the original exception accessible as `e.original_exception`.\n8. **Find an error handler** (line 943): `handler = self._find_error_handler(server_error, ctx.request.blueprints)` ΓÇö searches blueprint and app handlers for `InternalServerError`/`500`.\n9. **Call the handler if found** (lines 945ΓÇô946): `server_error = self.ensure_sync(handler)(server_error)`.\n10. **Finalize** (line 948): `return self.finalize_request(ctx, server_error, from_error_handler=True)` ΓÇö runs `make_response`, then `process_response` (which includes `after_request` hooks and `save_session`). The `from_error_handler=True` flag causes exceptions in finalization to be logged and swallowed rather than re-raised.\n\n---\n\n## Q9. Where is `ensure_sync` defined? What problem does it solve and what Python feature does it use?\n\n**Definition:** `src/flask/app.py`, lines 1065ΓÇô1077, method of class `Flask`.\n\n**The problem it solves:** Flask is a synchronous WSGI application. When a user defines an `async def` view function or hook, calling it directly would return a coroutine object rather than a response ΓÇö the coroutine would never be awaited. `ensure_sync` bridges the gap: it detects `async def` functions and wraps them so they are callable synchronously from WSGI code.\n\n**Python feature used:** `iscoroutinefunction(func)` from `inspect` (imported at the top of `app.py`). This checks whether `func` was declared with `async def`. If it was, `ensure_sync` delegates to `self.async_to_sync(func)` (lines 1079ΓÇô1100), which by default imports `asgiref.sync.async_to_sync` to run the coroutine in an event loop and block until it completes. Plain `def` functions are returned unchanged.\n\n```python\ndef ensure_sync(self, func):\n    if iscoroutinefunction(func):\n        return self.async_to_sync(func)\n    return func\n```\n\n`ensure_sync` is called before every view function, `before_request` handler, `after_request` handler, template context processor, error handler, and signal sender throughout the dispatch pipeline.\n\n---\n\n## Q10. Where is `make_response` defined? What types can it accept and how does it handle each?\n\n**Definition (primary):** `src/flask/app.py`, lines 1224ΓÇô1364, method of class `Flask`.\n**Also:** `src/flask/helpers.py`, lines 151ΓÇô197, a standalone helper function (calls `current_app.make_response()`).\n\n**Input types and handling:**\n\n| Type | Handling |\n|------|----------|\n| `tuple` (3-element) | Unpacked as `(body, status, headers)` |\n| `tuple` (2-element with `Headers`/`dict`/`tuple`/`list` second) | Unpacked as `(body, headers)` |\n| `tuple` (2-element with int/str second) | Unpacked as `(body, status)` |\n| `tuple` (other size) | Raises `TypeError` |\n| `None` | Raises `TypeError` (\"did not return a valid response\") |\n| `str` / `bytes` / `bytearray` | `self.response_class(rv, status=status, headers=headers)` ΓÇö creates Response with string/bytes body |\n| `cabc.Iterator` (generator/iterator) | Same as bytes/str ΓÇö streaming response |\n| `dict` or `list` | `self.json.response(rv)` ΓÇö JSON-serialized via the app's JSON provider |\n| `BaseResponse` (Werkzeug Response, not the app's subclass) | `self.response_class.force_type(rv, request.environ)` ΓÇö coerces to the app's response class |\n| callable (WSGI app) | `self.response_class.force_type(rv, request.environ)` ΓÇö evaluates the WSGI callable |\n| `self.response_class` instance | Returned unchanged |\n| Anything else | Raises `TypeError` |\n\nAfter normalization, if `status` is set, it updates `rv.status` (str) or `rv.status_code` (int). If `headers` is set, `rv.headers.update(headers)` extends the response headers.\n\n---\n\n## Q11. Trace from `Flask.__call__` to where the response is finalized. List every function in the chain.\n\n| Step | Function | File & Line |\n|------|----------|-------------|\n| 1 | `Flask.__call__(environ, start_response)` | `src/flask/app.py:1618` |\n| 2 | `Flask.wsgi_app(environ, start_response)` | `src/flask/app.py:1566` |\n| 3 | `Flask.request_context(environ)` ΓåÆ returns `AppContext` | called from `wsgi_app` line 1592 |\n| 4 | `AppContext.push()` | `src/flask/ctx.py:416` |\n| 5 | `AppContext._get_session()` (lazy, inside push) | `src/flask/ctx.py:381` |\n| 6 | `AppContext.match_request()` (inside push) | `src/flask/ctx.py:405` |\n| 7 | `Flask.full_dispatch_request(ctx)` | `src/flask/app.py:992` |\n| 8 | `request_started.send(...)` | `src/flask/app.py:1013` |\n| 9 | `Flask.preprocess_request(ctx)` | `src/flask/app.py:1366` |\n| 10 | `Flask.dispatch_request(ctx)` | `src/flask/app.py:966` |\n| 11 | `Flask.ensure_sync(view_func)(**view_args)` | `src/flask/app.py:990` |\n| 12 | `Flask.finalize_request(ctx, rv)` | `src/flask/app.py:1021` |\n| 13 | `Flask.make_response(rv)` | `src/flask/app.py:1224` |\n| 14 | `Flask.process_response(ctx, response)` | `src/flask/app.py:1394` |\n| 15 | `SessionInterface.save_session(app, session, response)` | `src/flask/app.py:1416` (called inside `process_response`) |\n| 16 | `request_finished.send(...)` | `src/flask/app.py:1042` |\n| 17 | `response(environ, start_response)` | `src/flask/app.py:1604` (back in `wsgi_app`) |\n| 18 | `AppContext.pop(error)` | `src/flask/ctx.py:446` (in `finally`) |\n\nIf an exception occurs at step 10/11, `handle_user_exception` or `handle_exception` is called instead, both of which ultimately call `finalize_request(..., from_error_handler=True)`.\n\n---\n\n## Q12. What is the exact chain when a session is saved at the end of a request? Trace from `save_session` being triggered to the cookie being written.\n\n1. **`Flask.finalize_request(ctx, rv)`** ΓÇö `src/flask/app.py:1021`. Calls `make_response(rv)` then calls `process_response`.\n2. **`Flask.process_response(ctx, response)`** ΓÇö `src/flask/app.py:1394`. Runs `after_request` handlers first, then on line 1415ΓÇô1416:\n   ```python\n   if not self.session_interface.is_null_session(ctx._get_session()):\n       self.session_interface.save_session(self, ctx._get_session(), response)\n   ```\n   `is_null_session()` checks if the session is an instance of `NullSession`. If not null, proceeds.\n3. **`ctx._get_session()`** ΓÇö `src/flask/ctx.py:381`. Returns the already-opened `SecureCookieSession` (or opens it if somehow not yet open).\n4. **`SecureCookieSessionInterface.save_session(app, session, response)`** ΓÇö `src/flask/sessions.py:337`. Reads all cookie attributes from config.\n5. **`self.get_signing_serializer(app)`** ΓÇö `src/flask/sessions.py:303`. Returns a `URLSafeTimedSerializer` configured with `app.secret_key`, `salt=\"cookie-session\"`, HMAC key derivation, SHA-1 digest.\n6. **`serializer.dumps(dict(session))`** ΓÇö serializes the session dict using `TaggedJSONSerializer` then signs with HMAC-SHA1, producing a URL-safe base64 string.\n7. **`response.set_cookie(name, val, expires=..., httponly=..., domain=..., path=..., secure=..., partitioned=..., samesite=...)`** ΓÇö Werkzeug `Response.set_cookie()`. This writes the `Set-Cookie` header into `response.headers`.\n8. **`response.vary.add(\"Cookie\")`** ΓÇö appends `Vary: Cookie` to the response headers.\n9. Back in `wsgi_app`, **`response(environ, start_response)`** ΓÇö the Werkzeug `Response.__call__` calls `start_response(status, headers)` with all headers (including `Set-Cookie`) and returns the body iterable, sending the cookie to the browser.\n\n---\n\n## Q13.
